style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">Architect</th><td style="border: 0;">\n<a href="/wiki/Richard_Morris_Hunt" title="Richard Morris Hunt">Richard Morris Hunt</a>; also <a href="/wiki/Calvert_Vaux" title="Calvert Vaux">Calvert Vaux</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Wrey_Mould" title="Jacob Wrey Mould">Jacob Wrey Mould</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: border: 0;">NRHP&#160;reference&#160;#</th><td style="border: 0;">\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://npgallery.nps.gov/AssetDetail/NRIS/86003556">86003556</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #A8EDEF">Significant dates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">Added to NRHP</th><td style="border: 0;">\nJanuary 29, 1972<sup id="cite_ref-nris_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nris-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">Designated&#160;NHL</th><td style="border: 0;">\n<p>June 24, 1986<sup id="cite_ref-nhlsum_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhlsum-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<sup id="cite_ref-2016wsj_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016wsj-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Metropolitan Museum of Art</b> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, colloquially "<b>the Met</b>",<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> is the largest art museum in the United States. With 7.06 million visitors in 2016, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_visited_art_museums" title="List of most visited art museums">third most visited art museum in the world</a>, and the fifth <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_visited_museums" title="List of most visited museums">most visited museum</a> of any kind.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Its permanent collection contains over two million works,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> divided among seventeen curatorial departments. The main building, on the eastern edge of <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> along <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue#Museum_Mile" title="Fifth Avenue">Museum Mile</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, is by area one of the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_art_museums" title="List of largest art museums">largest art galleries</a>. A much smaller second location, <a href="/wiki/The_Cloisters" title="The Cloisters">The Cloisters</a> at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Tryon_Park" title="Fort Tryon Park">Fort Tryon Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Manhattan" title="Upper Manhattan">Upper Manhattan</a>, contains an extensive collection of art, architecture, and artifacts from <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Europe">Medieval Europe</a>. On March 18, 2016, the museum opened the <a href="/wiki/Met_Breuer" title="Met Breuer">Met Breuer</a> museum at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Avenue" title="Madison Avenue">Madison Avenue</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a>; it extends the museum\'s modern and contemporary art program.\n</p><p>The permanent collection consists of works of art from <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_of_ancient_Egypt" title="Art of ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, paintings, and sculptures from nearly all the <a href="/wiki/Western_painting" title="Western painting">European</a> masters, and an extensive collection of <a href="/wiki/Visual_art_of_the_United_States" title="Visual art of the United States">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern</a> art. The Met maintains extensive holdings of <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian art">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceanian_art" title="Oceanian art">Oceanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">Byzantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic</a> art. The museum is home to encyclopedic collections of <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instruments</a>, costumes, and accessories, as well as antique <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armor" class="mw-redirect" title="Armor">armor</a> from around the world. Several notable interiors, ranging from first-century Rome through modern American design, are installed in its galleries.\n</p><p>The Metropolitan Museum of Art was founded in 1870 for the purposes of opening a museum to bring art and art education to the American people. It opened on February 20, 1872, and was originally located at 681 <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue" title="Fifth Avenue">Fifth Avenue</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Collections">Collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg/220px-The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg/330px-The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg/440px-The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="2047" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Great Hall.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s permanent collection is curated by seventeen separate departments, each with a specialized staff of <a href="/wiki/Curator" title="Curator">curators</a> and scholars, as well as six dedicated conservation departments and a Department of Scientific Research.<sup id="cite_ref-metsite_permanentcollection_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metsite_permanentcollection-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The permanent collection includes works of art from <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_of_ancient_Egypt" title="Art of ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, paintings and sculptures from nearly all the <a href="/wiki/Western_painting" title="Western painting">European</a> masters, and an extensive collection of <a href="/wiki/Visual_art_of_the_United_States" title="Visual art of the United States">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a>. The Met maintains extensive holdings of <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian art">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceanian_art" title="Oceanian art">Oceanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">Byzantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The museum is also home to encyclopedic collections of <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instruments</a>, costumes and accessories, and antique <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armor" class="mw-redirect" title="Armor">armor</a> from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> A great number of period rooms, ranging from <a href="/wiki/1st_century" title="1st century">1st century</a> Rome through modern American design, are permanently installed in the Met\'s galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In addition to its permanent exhibitions, the Met organizes and hosts large traveling shows throughout the year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The current chairman of the board, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Brodsky" title="Daniel Brodsky">Daniel Brodsky</a>, was elected in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-auto_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and became chairman three years after director <a href="/wiki/Philippe_de_Montebello" title="Philippe de Montebello">Philippe de Montebello</a> retired at the end of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-newme_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newme-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scur_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scur-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 March 2017, the BBC reported that <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Weiss_(art_historian)" title="Daniel Weiss (art historian)">Daniel Weiss</a>, the Met\'s president and <a href="/wiki/Chief_Operating_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Operating Officer">COO</a>, would also temporarily act as CEO for the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Following the departure of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_P._Campbell" title="Thomas P. Campbell">Thomas P. Campbell</a> as the Met\'s director and CEO on June 30, 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the search for a new director of the Museum was assigned to the human resources firm Phillips Oppenheim to present a new candidate for the position "by the end of the fiscal year in June" of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-nypogrebin_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nypogrebin-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The next director will report to Weiss as the current president of the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-https_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-https-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2018, <a href="/wiki/Max_Hollein" title="Max Hollein">Max Hollein</a> was named director.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collections:_Geographically_designated_collections">Collections: Geographically designated collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Collections: Geographically designated collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Near_Eastern_art">Ancient Near Eastern art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient Near Eastern art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Beginning in the late 19th century, the Met started acquiring ancient art and artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>. From a few <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a> tablets and <a href="/wiki/Seal_(device)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seal (device)">seals</a>, the Met\'s collection of Near Eastern art has grown to more than 7,000 pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Representing a history of the region beginning in the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> Period and encompassing the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a> and the end of <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a>, the collection includes works from the <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a>, Sasanian, <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elamite</a> cultures (among others), as well as an extensive collection of unique <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> objects. The highlights of the collection include a set of monumental stone <i><a href="/wiki/Lamassu" title="Lamassu">lamassu</a></i>, or guardian figures, from the Northwest Palace of the Assyrian king <a href="/wiki/Ashurnasirpal_II" title="Ashurnasirpal II">Ashurnasirpal II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Arts_of_Africa.2C_Oceania.2C_and_the_Americas"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_of_Africa,_Oceania,_and_the_Americas">Arts of Africa, Oceania, and the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Arts of Africa, Oceania, and the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg/220px-Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg" width="220" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg/330px-Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg/440px-Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1483" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Mother_Pendant_Mask-_Iyoba_MET_DP231460.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Benin_ivory_mask" title="Benin ivory mask">Benin ivory mask</a>, Iyoba, 16th century Nigeria</div></div></div>\n<p>Though the Met first acquired a group of Peruvian antiquities in 1882, the museum did not begin a concerted effort to collect works from Africa, Oceania, and the Americas until 1969, when American businessman and <a href="/wiki/Philanthropist" class="mw-redirect" title="Philanthropist">philanthropist</a> <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Rockefeller" title="Nelson Rockefeller">Nelson A. Rockefeller</a> donated his more than 3,000-piece collection to the museum. Today, the Met\'s collection contains more than 11,000 pieces from <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> and is housed in the 40,000-square-foot (4,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) Rockefeller Wing on the south end of the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The collection ranges from 40,000-year-old <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian_art#Rock_painting" title="Indigenous Australian art">indigenous Australian rock paintings</a>, to a group of 15-foot-tall (4.6&#160;m) memorial poles carved by the <a href="/wiki/Asmat_people" title="Asmat people">Asmat people</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, to a priceless collection of ceremonial and personal objects from the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> <a href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Benin Empire">Court of Benin</a> donated by <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Perls" title="Klaus Perls">Klaus Perls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ezra_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ezra-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The range of materials represented in the Africa, Oceania, and Americas collection is undoubtedly the widest of any department at the Met, including everything from precious metals to <a href="/wiki/Porcupine" title="Porcupine">porcupine</a> quills.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Asian_art">Asian art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Asian art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NatarajaMET.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/NatarajaMET.JPG/220px-NatarajaMET.JPG" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/NatarajaMET.JPG/330px-NatarajaMET.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/NatarajaMET.JPG/440px-NatarajaMET.JPG 2x" data-file-width="695" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NatarajaMET.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">Bronze</a> <a href="/wiki/Chola" class="mw-redirect" title="Chola">Chola</a> Statue of <i><a href="/wiki/Nataraja" title="Nataraja">Nataraja</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s Asian department holds a collection of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> art, of more than 35,000 pieces,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> that is arguably the most comprehensive in the US. The collection dates back almost to the founding of the museum: many of the philanthropists who made the earliest gifts to the museum included Asian art in their collections. Today, an entire wing of the museum is dedicated to the Asian collection, and spans 4,000 years of Asian art. Every Asian civilization is represented in the Met\'s Asian department, and the pieces on display include every type of decorative art, from painting and printmaking to sculpture and metalworking. The department is well known for its comprehensive collection of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_calligraphy" title="Chinese calligraphy">calligraphy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_painting" title="Chinese painting">painting</a>, as well as for its Indian sculptures, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepalese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibetan</a> works, and the arts of Burma (Myanmar), Cambodia and Thailand. All three ancient religions of India&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Hinduism, Buddhism and Jainism&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 are well represented in these sculptures.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> However, not only "art" and ritual objects are represented in the collection; many of the best-known pieces are functional objects. The Asian wing also contains a complete <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a>-style <a href="/wiki/Astor_Court" title="Astor Court">garden court</a>, modeled on a courtyard in the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_the_Nets_Garden" title="Master of the Nets Garden">Master of the Nets Garden</a> in <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>. Maxwell K. Hearn is the current department chairman of Asian Art since 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_art">Egyptian art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Egyptian art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg/220px-Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg/330px-Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg/440px-Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2899" data-file-height="2195" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Standing_Hippopotamus_MET_DP248993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_the_Faience_Hippopotamus" title="William the Faience Hippopotamus">William the Hippopotamus</a> is a mascot of the Met</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mummy,_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg/220px-Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg/330px-Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg/440px-Mummy%2C_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mummy,_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_NYC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mummy, Metropolitan Museum of Art NYC</div></div></div>\n<p>Though the majority of the Met\'s initial holdings of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> art came from private collections, items uncovered during the museum\'s own archeological excavations, carried out between 1906 and 1941, constitute almost half of the current collection. More than 26,000 separate pieces of Egyptian art from the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> era through the <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic</a> era constitute the Met\'s Egyptian collection, and almost all of them are on display in the museum\'s massive wing of 40 Egyptian galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  Among the most valuable pieces in the Met\'s Egyptian collection are 13 wooden models (of the total 24 models found together, 12 models and 1 offering bearer figure is at the Met, while the remaining 10 models and 1 offering bearer figure are in the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Egyptian Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>), discovered in a tomb in the Southern Asasif in western <a href="/wiki/Thebes,_Egypt" title="Thebes, Egypt">Thebes</a> in 1920. These models depict, in unparalleled detail, a cross-section of Egyptian life in the early <a href="/wiki/Middle_Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="Middle Kingdom of Egypt">Middle Kingdom</a>: boats, gardens, and scenes of daily life are represented in miniature. <a href="/wiki/William_the_Faience_Hippopotamus" title="William the Faience Hippopotamus">William the Faience Hippopotamus</a> is a miniature shown at right.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>However, the popular centerpiece of the Egyptian Art department continues to be the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Dendur" title="Temple of Dendur">Temple of Dendur</a>. Dismantled by the Egyptian government to save it from rising waters caused by the building of the <a href="/wiki/Aswan_High_Dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Aswan High Dam">Aswan High Dam</a>, the large <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> temple was given to the United States in 1965 and assembled in the Met\'s Sackler Wing in 1978. Situated in a large room and partially surrounded by a reflecting pool and illuminated by a wall of windows opening onto Central Park, the Temple of Dendur has been one of the Met\'s most enduring attractions. The oldest items at the Met, a set of Archeulian flints from <a href="/wiki/Deir_el-Bahri" class="mw-redirect" title="Deir el-Bahri">Deir el-Bahri</a> which date from the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a> period (between 300,000 and 75,000 BC), are part of the Egyptian collection. The curator is Diana Craig Patch.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_paintings">European paintings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European paintings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_(NYC,_USA).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG/310px-European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG" width="310" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG/465px-European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG/620px-European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_%28NYC%2C_USA%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4081" data-file-height="1248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_paintings_at_Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_(NYC,_USA).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European paintings at the museum.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s collection of European paintings numbers around 1,700 pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The current Chairman of the European Paintings is Keith Christianson who has been at the museum since 1977.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_sculpture_and_decorative_arts">European sculpture and decorative arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: European sculpture and decorative arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg/220px-NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg/330px-NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg/440px-NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NYC_-_Metropolitan_Museum_-_Carroll_and_Milton_Petrie_European_Sculpture_Court.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European sculpture court.</div></div></div>\n<p>The European Sculpture and Decorative Arts collection is one of the largest departments at the Met, holding in excess of 50,000 separate pieces from the <a href="/wiki/15th_century" title="15th century">15th</a> through the early <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th centuries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Although the collection is particularly concentrated in Renaissance sculpture\xe2\x80\x94much of which can be seen <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ" title="In situ">in situ</a></i> surrounded by contemporary furnishings and decoration\xe2\x80\x94it also contains comprehensive holdings of furniture, jewelry, glass and ceramic pieces, tapestries, textiles, and timepieces and mathematical instruments. In addition to its outstanding collections of English and French furniture, visitors can enter dozens of completely furnished period rooms, transplanted in their entirety into the Met\'s galleries. The collection even includes an entire <a href="/wiki/16th_century" title="16th century">16th century</a> <a href="/wiki/Patio" title="Patio">patio</a> from the Spanish castle of <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9lez_Blanco" class="mw-redirect" title="V\xc3\xa9lez Blanco">V\xc3\xa9lez Blanco</a>, reconstructed in a two-story gallery, and the intarsia <i><a href="/wiki/Studiolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Studiolo">studiolo</a></i> from the ducal palace at Gubbio. Sculptural highlights of the sprawling department include <a href="/wiki/Bernini" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernini">Bernini</a>\'s <i>Bacchanal</i>, a cast of <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Rodin\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Burghers_of_Calais" title="The Burghers of Calais">The Burghers of Calais</a></i>, and several unique pieces by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Antoine_Houdon" title="Jean-Antoine Houdon">Houdon</a>, including his <i>Bust of <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a></i> and his famous portrait of his daughter Sabine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Wing">American Wing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: American Wing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze,_MMA-NYC,_1851.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/220px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/330px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/440px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6004" data-file-height="3847" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze,_MMA-NYC,_1851.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware" title="Washington Crossing the Delaware">Washington Crossing the Delaware</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">Emanuel Leutze</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The museum\'s collection of American art returned to view in new galleries on January 16, 2012. The new installation provides visitors with the history of American art from the 18th through the early 20th century. The new galleries encompasses 30,000 square feet (2,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) for the display of the museum\'s collection.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The curator in charge of the American Wing since September 2014 is Sylvia Yount.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_and_Roman_art">Greek and Roman art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Greek and Roman art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg/220px-Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg/330px-Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg/440px-Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_the_New_Roman_Gallery_at_the_Metropolitan%E2%80%94New_York_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greek and Roman gallery</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s collection of Greek and Roman art contains more than 17,000 objects.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Greek and Roman collection dates back to the founding of the museum\xe2\x80\x94in fact, the museum\'s first accessioned object was a Roman <a href="/wiki/Sarcophagus" title="Sarcophagus">sarcophagus</a>, still currently on display. Though the collection naturally concentrates on items from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, these historical regions represent a wide range of cultures and artistic styles, from classic Greek <a href="/wiki/Black-figure_pottery" title="Black-figure pottery">black-figure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red-figure_pottery" title="Red-figure pottery">red-figure</a> vases to carved Roman <a href="/wiki/Tunic" title="Tunic">tunic</a> pins.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg/220px-Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg/330px-Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg/440px-Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1905" data-file-height="1525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Limestone_sarcophagus-_the_Amathus_sarcophagus_MET_DT352.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Amathus_sarcophagus" title="Amathus sarcophagus">Amathus sarcophagus</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Amathus" title="Amathus">Amathus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, arguably the single most important object in the Cesnola Collection</div></div></div>\n<p>Highlights of the collection include the monumental <a href="/wiki/Amathus_sarcophagus" title="Amathus sarcophagus">Amathus sarcophagus</a> and a magnificently detailed Etruscan chariot known as the "<a href="/wiki/Monteleone_chariot" title="Monteleone chariot">Monteleone chariot</a>". The collection also contains many pieces from far earlier than the Greek or Roman empires\xe2\x80\x94among the most remarkable are a collection of early <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cycladic</a> sculptures from the mid-third millennium BC, many so abstract as to seem almost modern. The Greek and Roman galleries also contain several large classical wall paintings and reliefs from different periods, including an entire reconstructed bedroom from a noble <a href="/wiki/Villa" title="Villa">villa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boscoreale" title="Boscoreale">Boscoreale</a>, excavated after its entombment by the eruption of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vesuvius" title="Mount Vesuvius">Vesuvius</a> in AD 79. In 2007, the Met\'s Greek and Roman galleries were expanded to approximately 60,000 square feet (6,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), allowing the majority of the collection to be on permanent display.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_greekroman_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_greekroman-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_art">Islamic art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Islamic art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg/220px-Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg/330px-Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg/440px-Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3791" data-file-height="2581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Folio_Blue_Quran_Met_2004.88.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaf from the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Qur%27an" title="Blue Qur&#39;an">Blue Qur\'an</a> showing Chapter 30: 28\xe2\x80\x9332</div></div></div>\n<p>The Metropolitan Museum owns one of the world\'s largest collection of works of art of the Islamic world. The collection also includes artifacts and works of art of cultural and secular origin from the time period indicated by the rise of Islam predominantly from the Near East and in contrast to the Ancient Near Eastern collections. The biggest number of miniatures from the "Shahnama" list prepared under the reign of Shah Tahmasp I, the most luxurious of all the existing Islamic manuscripts, also belongs to this museum. Other rarities include the works of Sultan Muhammad and his associates from the Tabriz school "The Sade Holiday", "Tahmiras kills divs", "Bijan and Manizhe", and many others.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Met\'s collection of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a> is not confined strictly to <a href="/wiki/Religious_art" title="Religious art">religious art</a>, though a significant number of the objects in the Islamic collection were originally created for religious use or as decorative elements in <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a>. Much of the 12,000 strong collection consists of secular items, including ceramics and <a href="/wiki/Textiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Textiles">textiles</a>, from Islamic cultures ranging from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Islamic Art department\'s collection of miniature paintings from <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal India</a> are a highlight of the collection. <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">Calligraphy</a> both religious and secular is well represented in the Islamic Art department, from the official decrees of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a> to a number of <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur&#39;an">Qur\'an</a> manuscripts reflecting different periods and styles of calligraphy. Modern calligraphic artists also used a word or phrase to convey a direct message, or they created compositions from the shapes of Arabic words. Others incorporated indecipherable cursive writing within the body of the work to evoke the illusion of writing.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Islamic Arts galleries had been undergoing refurbishment since 2001 and were reopened on November 1, 2011, as the New Galleries for the Art of the Arab Lands, Turkey, Iran, Central Asia, and Later South Asia. Until that time, a narrow selection of items from the collection had been on temporary display throughout the museum. As with many other departments at the Met, the Islamic Art galleries contain many interior pieces, including the entire reconstructed <i>Nur Al-Din Room</i> from an early 18th-century house in <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>. However, the museum has confirmed to the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i> that it has withdrawn from public display all paintings depicting Muhammad and may not rehang those that were displayed in the Islamic gallery before the renovation.<sup id="cite_ref-nypost.com_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nypost.com-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collections:_Non-geographically_designated_collections">Collections: Non-geographically designated collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Collections: Non-geographically designated collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms_and_Armor">Arms and Armor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Arms and Armor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg/220px-Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg/330px-Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg/440px-Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1995" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Middle_Age_Main_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arms and armor, Middle Ages main hall</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s Department of Arms and Armor is one of the museum\'s most popular collections.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The distinctive "parade" of armored figures on horseback installed in the first-floor Arms and Armor gallery is one of the most recognizable images of the museum, which was organized in 1975 with the help of the Russian immigrant and arms and armors\' scholar, Leonid Tarassuk (1925\xe2\x80\x9390). The department\'s focus on "outstanding craftsmanship and decoration," including pieces intended solely for display, means that the collection is strongest in <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">late medieval</a> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> pieces and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> pieces from the 5th through the 19th centuries. However, these are not the only cultures represented in Arms and Armor; the collection spans more geographic regions than almost any other department, including weapons and armor from <a href="/wiki/Early_Dynastic_Period_of_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Dynastic Period of Egypt">dynastic Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, the ancient <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, as well as American firearms (especially <a href="/wiki/Colt%27s_Manufacturing_Company" title="Colt&#39;s Manufacturing Company">Colt</a> firearms) from the 19th and 20th centuries. Among the collection\'s 14,000 objects<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> are many pieces made for and used by kings and princes, including armor belonging to <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand I of Germany">Ferdinand I of Germany</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Costume_Institute">Costume Institute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Costume Institute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anna_Wintour_Costume_Center" title="Anna Wintour Costume Center">Anna Wintour Costume Center</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg/220px-Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg/330px-Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg/440px-Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robe_%C3%A0_la_Fran%C3%A7aise_MET_DT3884.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Robe \xc3\xa0 la fran\xc3\xa7aise 1740s, as seen in one of the exhibits at the Costume Institute.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Museum of Costume Art was founded by <a href="/wiki/Aline_Bernstein" title="Aline Bernstein">Aline Bernstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irene_Lewisohn" title="Irene Lewisohn">Irene Lewisohn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 1937, they merged with the Met and became its Costume Institute department. Today, its collection contains more than 35,000 costumes and accessories.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The Costume Institute used to have a permanent gallery space in what was known as the "Basement" area of the Met because it was downstairs at the bottom of the Met facility. However, due to the fragile nature of the items in the collection, the Costume Institute does not maintain a permanent installation. Instead, every year it holds two separate shows in the Met\'s galleries using costumes from its collection, with each show centering on a specific designer or theme. The Costume Institute is known for hosting the annual <a href="/wiki/Met_Gala" title="Met Gala">Met Gala</a> and in the past has presented summer exhibitions such as <a href="/wiki/Savage_Beauty_(exhibition)" title="Savage Beauty (exhibition)">Savage Beauty</a> and <a href="/wiki/China:_Through_the_Looking_Glass" title="China: Through the Looking Glass">China: Through the Looking Glass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trebay_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trebay-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tomkins_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tomkins-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In past years, Costume Institute shows organized around famous designers such as <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_Balenciaga" title="Crist\xc3\xb3bal Balenciaga">Crist\xc3\xb3bal Balenciaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">Chanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yves_Saint_Laurent_(designer)" title="Yves Saint Laurent (designer)">Yves Saint Laurent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace" title="Gianni Versace">Gianni Versace</a>; and style doyenne like <a href="/wiki/Diana_Vreeland" title="Diana Vreeland">Diana Vreeland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mona_von_Bismarck" title="Mona von Bismarck">Mona von Bismarck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babe_Paley" title="Babe Paley">Babe Paley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jayne_Wrightsman" title="Jayne Wrightsman">Jayne Wrightsman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nan_Kempner" title="Nan Kempner">Nan Kempner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iris_Apfel" title="Iris Apfel">Iris Apfel</a> have drawn significant crowds to the Met. The <a href="/wiki/Met_Ball" class="mw-redirect" title="Met Ball">Costume Institute\'s annual Benefit Gala</a>, co-chaired by <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i> editor-in-chief <a href="/wiki/Anna_Wintour" title="Anna Wintour">Anna Wintour</a>, is an extremely popular, if exclusive, event in the fashion world; in 2007, the 700 available tickets started at $6,500 per person.<sup id="cite_ref-postrel_dress_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-postrel_dress-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\nExhibits displayed over the past decade in the Costume Institute include: Rock Style, in 1999, representing the style of more than 40 rock musicians, including <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>; Extreme Beauty: The Body Transformed, in 2001, which exposes the transforming ideas of physical beauty over time and the bodily contortion necessary to accommodate such ideals and fashion; The <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">Chanel</a> Exhibit, displayed in 2005, acknowledging the skilled work of designer <a href="/wiki/Coco_Chanel" title="Coco Chanel">Coco Chanel</a> as one of the leading fashion names in history; Superheroes: Fashion and Fantasy, exhibited in 2008, suggesting the metaphorical vision of superheroes as ultimate fashion icons; the 2010 exhibit on the American Woman: Fashioning a National Identity, which exposes the revolutionary styles of the American woman from the years 1890 to 1940, and how such styles reflect the political and social sentiments of the time. The theme of the 2011 event was "Alexander McQueen: <a href="/wiki/Savage_Beauty_(exhibition)" title="Savage Beauty (exhibition)">Savage Beauty</a>". Each of these exhibits explores fashion as a mirror of cultural values and offers a glimpse into historical styles, emphasizing their evolution into today\'s own fashion world. On January 14, 2014, the Met named the Costume Institute complex after <a href="/wiki/Anna_Wintour" title="Anna Wintour">Anna Wintour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The curator is <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bolton_(curator)" title="Andrew Bolton (curator)">Andrew Bolton</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drawings_and_prints">Drawings and prints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Drawings and prints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg/220px-D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg" width="220" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg/330px-D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg/440px-D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3146" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCrer_Melancholia_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Melencolia_I" title="Melencolia I">Melencolia I</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer">Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Though other departments contain significant numbers of <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">drawings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Printmaking" title="Printmaking">prints</a>, the Drawings and Prints department specifically concentrates on <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> pieces and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western European</a> works produced after the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. The first Old Master drawings, comprising 670 sheets, were presented as a single group in 1880 by <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Vanderbilt_II" title="Cornelius Vanderbilt II">Cornelius Vanderbilt II</a> and in effect launched the department, though it was not formally constituted as a department until later. Other early donors to the department include <a href="/wiki/Junius_Spencer_Morgan_II" title="Junius Spencer Morgan II">Junius Spencer Morgan II</a> who presented a broad range of material, but mainly dated from the sixteenth century, including 2 woodblocks and many prints by <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer">Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer</a> in 1919. Currently, the Drawings and Prints collection contains more than 17,000 drawings, 1.5 million prints, and twelve thousand illustrated books.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The great masters of European painting, who produced many more sketches and drawings than actual paintings, are extensively represented in the Drawing and Prints collection. The department\'s holdings contain major drawings by <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, as well as prints and etchings by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Dyck" title="Anthony van Dyck">Van Dyck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer">D\xc3\xbcrer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Degas" title="Edgar Degas">Degas</a> among many others. The curator is Nadine Orenstein.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Robert_Lehman_Collection">Robert Lehman Collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Robert Lehman Collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG/220px-Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG/330px-Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG/440px-Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Lehman_Wing_-_Visitors_Watching_Impressionist_Masters.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Robert Lehman Wing</div></div></div>\n<p>On the death of banker <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lehman" title="Robert Lehman">Robert Lehman</a> in 1969, his Foundation donated 2,600 works of art to the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Housed in the "Robert Lehman Wing," the museum refers to the collection as "one of the most extraordinary private art collections ever assembled in the United States".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> To emphasize the personal nature of the Robert Lehman Collection, the Met housed the collection in a special set of galleries which evoked the interior of Lehman\'s richly decorated <a href="/wiki/Townhouse" title="Townhouse">townhouse</a>; this intentional separation of the Collection as a "museum within the museum" met with mixed criticism and approval at the time, though the acquisition of the collection was seen as a coup for the Met.<sup id="cite_ref-ThomasHoving_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThomasHoving-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Unlike other departments at the Met, the Robert Lehman collection does not concentrate on a specific style or period of art; rather, it reflects Lehman\'s personal interests. Lehman the collector concentrated heavily on paintings of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Siena" title="Siena">Sienese</a> school. Paintings in the collection include masterpieces by <a href="/wiki/Botticelli" class="mw-redirect" title="Botticelli">Botticelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Veneziano" title="Domenico Veneziano">Domenico Veneziano</a>, as well as works by a significant number of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> painters, <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Goya" title="Francisco Goya">Goya</a> among them. Lehman\'s collection of drawings by the <a href="/wiki/Old_Masters" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Masters">Old Masters</a>, featuring works by <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht D\xc3\xbcrer">D\xc3\xbcrer</a>, is particularly valuable for its breadth and quality.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University_Press" title="Princeton University Press">Princeton University Press</a> has documented the massive collection in a multi-volume book series published as <i>The Robert Lehman Collection Catalogues</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_art_and_the_Cloisters">Medieval art and the Cloisters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Medieval art and the Cloisters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pol,_Jean,_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg/170px-Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg/255px-Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg/340px-Pol%2C_Jean%2C_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="586" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pol,_Jean,_and_Herman_de_Limbourg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Limbourg_brothers" title="Limbourg brothers">Limbourg brothers</a>\' <i><a href="/wiki/Belles_Heures_of_Jean_de_France,_Duc_de_Berry" title="Belles Heures of Jean de France, Duc de Berry">Belles Heures of Jean de France, Duc de Berry</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s collection of medieval art consists of a comprehensive range of Western art from the 4th through the early 16th centuries, as well as <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">Byzantine</a> and pre-medieval European antiquities not included in the Ancient Greek and Roman collection. Like the Islamic collection, the Medieval collection contains a broad range of two- and three-dimensional art, with religious objects heavily represented. In total, the Medieval Art department\'s permanent collection numbers about 11,000 separate objects, divided between the main museum building on Fifth Avenue and <a href="/wiki/The_Cloisters" title="The Cloisters">The Cloisters</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_building">Main building</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Main building">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>The medieval collection in the main Metropolitan building, centered on the first-floor medieval gallery, contains about six thousand separate objects. While a great deal of European medieval art is on display in these galleries, most of the European pieces are concentrated at the Cloisters (see below). However, this allows the main galleries to display much of the Met\'s Byzantine art side-by-side with European pieces. The main gallery is host to a wide range of tapestries and church and funerary statuary, while side galleries display smaller works of precious metals and ivory, including <a href="/wiki/Reliquary" title="Reliquary">reliquary</a> pieces and secular items. The main gallery, with its high arched ceiling, also serves double duty as the annual site of the Met\'s elaborately decorated Christmas tree.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Cloisters_museum_and_gardens">The Cloisters museum and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The Cloisters museum and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Cloisters" title="The Cloisters">The Cloisters</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg/260px-The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg" width="260" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg/390px-The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg/520px-The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2648" data-file-height="1373" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cloisters_Hudson_River_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Cloisters" title="The Cloisters">The Cloisters</a> from the Hudson River</div></div></div>\n<p>The Cloisters was a principal project of <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="John D. Rockefeller, Jr.">John D. Rockefeller, Jr.</a>, a major benefactor of the Met. Located in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Tryon_Park" title="Fort Tryon Park">Fort Tryon Park</a> and completed in 1938, it is a separate building dedicated solely to medieval art. The Cloisters collection was originally that of a separate museum, assembled by <a href="/wiki/George_Grey_Barnard" title="George Grey Barnard">George Grey Barnard</a> and acquired <i>in toto</i> by Rockefeller in 1925 as a gift to the Met.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Cloisters are so named on account of the five medieval French <a href="/wiki/Cloisters" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloisters">cloisters</a> whose salvaged structures were incorporated into the modern building, and the five thousand objects at the Cloisters are strictly limited to medieval European works. The collection features items of outstanding beauty and historical importance; including the <i><a href="/wiki/Belles_Heures_of_Jean_de_France,_Duc_de_Berry" title="Belles Heures of Jean de France, Duc de Berry">Belles Heures of Jean de France, Duc de Berry</a></i> illustrated by the <a href="/wiki/Limbourg_Brothers" class="mw-redirect" title="Limbourg Brothers">Limbourg Brothers</a> in 1409, the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a> altar cross known as the "<a href="/wiki/Cloisters_Cross" title="Cloisters Cross">Cloisters Cross</a>" or "Bury Cross", and the seven <a href="/wiki/Tapestry" title="Tapestry">tapestries</a> depicting the <a href="/wiki/The_Hunt_of_the_Unicorn" title="The Hunt of the Unicorn">Hunt of the Unicorn</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_and_contemporary_art">Modern and contemporary art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Modern and contemporary art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>With some 13,000 artworks, primarily by European and American artists, the modern art collection occupies 60,000 square feet (6,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), of gallery space and contains many iconic modern works. Cornerstones of the collection include <a href="/wiki/Picasso" class="mw-redirect" title="Picasso">Picasso</a>\'s portrait of <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Stein" title="Gertrude Stein">Gertrude Stein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Johns" title="Jasper Johns">Jasper Johns</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/White_Flag_(Johns_painting)" title="White Flag (Johns painting)">White Flag</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Pollock" title="Jackson Pollock">Jackson Pollock</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Autumn_Rhythm_(Number_30)" title="Autumn Rhythm (Number 30)">Autumn Rhythm (Number 30)</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Max_Beckmann" title="Max Beckmann">Max Beckmann</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Triptych" title="Triptych">triptych</a> <i>Beginning</i>. Certain artists are represented in remarkable depth, for a museum whose focus is not exclusively on modern art: for example, the collection contains forty paintings by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Klee" title="Paul Klee">Paul Klee</a>, spanning his entire career. Due to the Met\'s long history, "contemporary" paintings acquired in years past have often migrated to other collections at the museum, particularly to the American and European Paintings departments.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In April 2013, it was reported that the museum was to receive a collection worth $1 billion from cosmetics tycoon <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Lauder" title="Leonard Lauder">Leonard Lauder</a>. The collection of <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubist</a> art includes work by Pablo Picasso, Georges Braque and Juan Gris and went on display in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_instruments">Musical instruments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Musical instruments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg/220px-Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg/330px-Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg/440px-Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3893" data-file-height="2905" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Pianoforte_MET_DP225545.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grand piano by <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_%C3%89rard" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien \xc3\x89rard">S\xc3\xa9bastien \xc3\x89rard</a>, ~1840</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s collection of musical instruments, with about 5,000 examples of musical instruments from all over the world, is virtually unique among major museums.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>  The collection began in 1889 with a donation of 270 instruments by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Elizabeth_Adams_Brown" title="Mary Elizabeth Adams Brown">Mary Elizabeth Adams Brown</a>, who joined her collection to become the museum\'s first curator of musical instruments, named in honor of her husband, <a href="/wiki/John_Crosby_Brown" title="John Crosby Brown">John Crosby Brown</a>. By the time she died, the collection had 3,600 instruments that she had donated and the collection was housed in five galleries. Instruments were (and continue to be) included in the collection not only on aesthetic grounds, but also insofar as they embodied technical and social aspects of their cultures of origin. The modern Musical Instruments collection is encyclopedic in scope; every continent is represented at virtually every stage of its musical life. Highlights of the department\'s collection include several <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Stradivari" title="Antonio Stradivari">Stradivari</a> <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violins</a>, a collection of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> instruments made from precious metals, and the oldest surviving <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a>, a 1720 model by <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeo_Cristofori" title="Bartolomeo Cristofori">Bartolomeo Cristofori</a>. Many of the instruments in the collection are playable, and the department encourages their use by holding concerts and demonstrations by guest musicians.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Photographs">Photographs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Photographs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg/220px-La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg/330px-La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg/440px-La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2875" data-file-height="3837" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Tour_St._Jacques_La_Boucherie_%C3%A0_Paris_ca._1867.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>La Tour St. Jacques La Boucherie \xc3\xa0 Paris</i> by Charles Soulier, 1867.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Met\'s collection of <a href="/wiki/Photograph" title="Photograph">photographs</a>, numbering more than 25,000 in total,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> is centered on five major collections plus additional acquisitions by the museum. <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Stieglitz" title="Alfred Stieglitz">Alfred Stieglitz</a>, a famous photographer himself, donated the first major collection of photographs to the museum, which included a comprehensive survey of <a href="/wiki/Pictorialism" title="Pictorialism">Photo-Secessionist</a> works, a rich set of master prints by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Steichen" title="Edward Steichen">Edward Steichen</a>, and an outstanding collection of Stieglitz\'s photographs from his own studio.
